thus vnfolde ſorrowes greatly bewayle fortune beholde harde great noyes crie doore came magiſtrates officer cōmaunded twoo ſergeantes binde leade pryſon whereunto willingly obedient ledde thorough ſtreate citie gathered together followed although looked alwaies grounde ſhame yet ſometimes caſt head aſide merueled greatly amongſt ſo many thouſand people one laughed excéedingly finally brought thorough ſtréetes citie mā ner thoſe goe proceſſion doo ſacrafice mitigate ire god placed iudgemēt hall ſeate iudges crier cōmaunded men kéepe ſilence people deſired iudges giue ſentence great theatre reaſon y• great multitude wherby thei weare daunger ſtifling beholde y• preaſe people encreaſed ſtil ſome climed toppe houſe ſome gotte vpon beames ſome vpō image ſome thruſt heades windowes litle regardyng daunger ſo might ſee officer brought forth opēly midle hall y• euery man might beholde crier made oies willed ſuche would bringe euidence againſt ſhoulde come forth ſtepped olde man glaſſe water hande droppyng ſoftly deſired might haue libertie ſpeake duringe time continuance water graunted beganne oration ſorte ¶how apuleius accuſed olde man anſweared ſelfe cap 13 moſt reuerēde iuſt iudges thinge purpoſe declare vnto ſmal matter toucheth eſtate tranquillitie whole citie puniſhment therof may right good example others wherefore pray moſte venerable father whome euery whome doth appertaine prouide dignitie ſafetie common weale would wiſe ſuffer wicked homicide embrewed bloud ſo many murdred citizen ſcape vnpuniſhed thinke y• moued hereunto enuie hatred reaſon mine office y• capitaine night watche becauſe man aliue ſhould accuſe remiſſe ſame declare whole matter orderly done laſt night night paſt accuſtomed howre ithe inuectiue 〈◊〉 againſt apuleius diligently ſearched euery parte citie behold fortuned eſpie cruell yonge man drawinge ſwoorde againſt thrée citizen longe combate foughten betwene murdred one miſerably whē done moued conſcience ſo great crime ranne away ayded reaſon darkenes ſlipt houſe lay hidden night prouidence god ſuffereth heynous offence remaine vnpuniſhed takē v morninge eſcaped ſo brought hither honorable preſence receaue deſert accordingly haue giltie perſon culpable homicide accuſed ſtraunger wherefore pronounce ye iudgement againſt man alien would moſt ſeuerely ſharpely reuenge ſuch offence found knowen citizen ſort y• cruel accuſer finiſhed ended terrible tale crier commaunded ſpeake thinge ſay ſelfe could wiſe vtter woorde wéepinge ſide eſtéemed ſo much rigorous accuſation conſider mine owne miſerable conſcience howbeit beinge inſpired diuine audacitie length ganne ſaythe anſweare apuleius verely know hard thinge accuſed haue ſlayne thrée perſons perſuade innocent although ſhould declare whole truth confeſſe matter déede honour vouchſalue giue audience ſhow cōdemned die haue deſerued mine owne deſerte moued fortune reaſonable cauſe doo facte returninge ſomewhat late ſupper yeſternight beinge well tippled wine whiche denie approchinge nighe vnto common lodginge houſe one milo citizen citie fortuned eſpie thrée great théeues attemptinge breake downe walles gate open locke enter whē remoued doores hooke thei conſulted emongſt ſelues would hādle ſuch founde houſe one beyng courage greater ſtature reſt ſpake vnto fellowes ſaide tuſhe boyes take men harte vnto let v enter euery parte houſe ſuche finde ſléepe let v ſlea ſuch likewiſe reſiſt let v kill ſo meanes ſhall eſcape without daunger verely ye iudges confeſſe drew ſwoorde againſt thoſe thrée citizen thought office duetie one heareth good weale publique ſo doo ſpecially ſince put great feare aſſayed robbe ſpoile mine hoſte milo thoſe cruell terrible men woulde caſe rūne away feare naked ſwoorde boldly reſiſt againſt ranne vpō fought valiantly one capitaine inuaded ſtrongly drewe heare handes beganne beate great ſtone ende proued hardier man threwe downe féete killed toke likewiſe ſeconde claſped legges bitte ſlewe alſo thirde came running violently againſt ſtrokē vnder ſtomake fell downe dead thus deliuered ſelfe houſe mine hoſte familie preſent daunger thought ſhould onely eſcape vnpuniſhed alſo haue ſome great rewarde citie paine moreouer haue alwaies béene cléere vnſpotted crime haue eſtéemed mine innocencie aboue treaſure worlde finde reaſonable cauſe vpon mine accuſation ſhould condemned die ſince firſt moued ſet vpō théeues iuſt occaſion secondly becauſe none affirme hath bene time either grudge hatred betwene v thirdly men mere ſtraungers acquaintance laſt man proue committed facte lucre gaine ended woordes ſort beholde wéeped againe pitiouſly holdinge vp handes prayed people mercie cō mon weale loue poore infantes child ſhowe ſome pitie fauour whē ſawe harte ſomewhat relented moued lamentable teares called goddes witneſſe vngiltie crime ſo diuine prouidence committed preſent eſtate turninge ſelfe againe perceaued people laughed encéedingly eſpecially good fréende hoſte milo thought ſelfe ala faith remorſe cōſcience beholde condemned die murderer ſaluegarde mine hoſte milo familie yet contented y• likewiſe laugheth ſkorne otherwiſe ſhould comfort helpe ¶how apuleius accuſed twoo woman ſlaine body founde blowen bladder cap 14 done came woman wepinge middle theatre arrayed mourninge veſture bearinge childe armes came olde woman ragged robe cryinge howlinge likewiſe thei brought thē oliue bowes wherwith thrée ſlaine body couered biere cried māner right iudges pray iuſtice humanitie whiche haue mercie vpon theſe ſlaine perſons ſuccour widowhed loſſe déere huſbandes eſpecially poore infant orphan depriued good fortune execute iuſtice order lawe vpon bloud théefe occaſion ſorowes ſpokē theſe woordes one moſt auncient iudges riſe ſay touchinge murder deſerueth great puniſhment malefactor ſelfe cānot denie dutie enquire trie whether coadiutors help likely one man alone could kill thrée ſuch great valiant perſons wherefore truth muſt tried y• racke ſo ſhall learne compaignions hath coote neſt theſe miſcheuous murderer long delay accordinge vnto cuſtome grecia fire whele many tormentes brought thē ſorow encreaſed rather doubled y• could ende life whole vnperiſhed mēbers olde woman troubled courte howling deſired iudges ſhould tormented racke might vncouer body ſlaine y• euery man might ſée comely ſhape youthfull beautie might receaue condigne woorthy puniſhment according y• qualitie offence therewithall ſhe made ſigne ioye y• iudge cōmaūded foorthwith diſcouer body ſlaine liynge vpon biere mine owne handes whē refuſed good ſpace reaſon would make facte apparant eies men ſergeantes charged cōmaundement iudges thruſt forwarde doo ſame beyng enforced neceſſitie though weare againſt vncouered body good lord ſtraunge ſight ſée monſter ſodeine chaunge ſorrowes ſéemed though weare one houſe proſerpina familie death ſo much y• could ſufficiently expreſſe y• forme new ſight ſo far amaſed aſtonied thereat body y• thrée ſlaine men body thrée blowen bladder mangled diuers place ſéemed wounded thoſe partes remember wounded théeues night whereat people laughed excéedingely reioyſed meruelouſly remembraunce thereof ſome helde ſtomakes aked ioye euery mā delighted paſſyng ſporte ſo departed theatre time vncouered body ſtoode ſtill cold iſe otherwiſe ſtatues image neither came vnto right ſenſes vntill ſuch time milo mine hoſte came toke • hād ciuill violence ledde away wepinge ſobbinge would becauſe might ſéene brought many blind way lane houſe wente comfort beinge ſadde yet fearefull gentle entreatie talke coulde wiſe mitigate impaciencie iniurie whiche conceiued within minde behold magiſtrates iudges enſignes entred houſe endeuored pacifie ſorte ſaying lucius aduertiſed dignitie know genelogie auncient lignage nobilitie kinne doo poſſeſſe greateſt parte al province thinke haue ſuffred thinge wherefore wéepe reproche ignominie put away care ſorrowe minde day whiche celebrate yéere honour god riſus alwaies renoumpned ſome ſolempne nouell god doth cōtinually accōpanie inuentor thereof ſuffer ſhould ſorowfull pleaſantly beare ioyfull face verely al citie grace entende rewarde great honour make patron ſtatue image ſhalbe ſet vp perpetuall remembraunce whome anſweared ſuche benefites haue receaued alreadie famous citie theſſalie yéelde render moſte entier thankes • ouchinge ſettinge vp ſtatues image would wiſhe ſhould reſerued mine aū cientes ſuch woorthy ſpoken theſe woordes ſomewhat grauely ſhowed ſelf nore merry iudges magiſtrates departed reuerently toke leaue bidde farewell beholde came one runnyng haſt ſaid sir coſin birrhena deſireth take paine accordinge promiſe yeſternight come ſupper ready greatly fearing goe houſe night ſaid vnto y• meſſenger fréende pray tell coſin miſteris would willingly commaūdement breakinge troth credite mine hoſte milo enforced aſſure cōpelled feaw preſent day ſhould departe companie wherefore pray excuſe differ promiſe time ſpeakinge theſe woordes milo toke hande ledde towardes next baine way went couchinge vnder hide ſelfe ſight men becauſe miniſtred ſuch occaſion laughter waſhed wiped ſelfe returned home againe neuer remembred ſuch thing ſo greatly aſhamed noddinge pointyng euery perſon went ſupper milo god wotte fared poorely wherefore feigninge head ake reaſon ſobbinge weping daie deſired licence departe chamber ſo went bedde ¶how fotis tolde apuleius witchcratie miſtris vſe cap 15 bedde beganne cal minde al ſorrowes griefes day vntill ſuch time loue fotis hauinge brought miſtris ſléepe came chamber ſhe wonte doo ſhe ſéemed nothinge pleaſant neither countenance talke ſower face frowning looke gan ſpeake ſorte verely confeſſe haue bene occaſion thy trouble day therewithall ſhe pulled whippe vnder apron deliuered ſaying commaundement wrought thought ſome beholde vnlucky chaunce fortuned mine euil occaſion curious deſirous know matter anſweared faith ꝙ moſte peſtilent euill fauoured whippe whiche thou haſt brought ſcourge thée withall ſhall firſte broken thouſande piece ſhould touch hurte thy delicate deintie ſkinne pray tell haue bene cauſe meane trouble ſorrowe dare ſweare loue beare vnto perſwaded though ſelfe ſhoulde endeuour ſame euer wente trouble harme perhappes ſometimes imagined euill thought minde whiche afterwardes reuoked déemed crime ſpoken theſe woordes perceaued fotis eies beinge wette teares welnie cloſed vp ſhe deſire vnto pleaſure ſpecially becauſe ſhe embraced kiſſed ſwéetely ſhe ſomwhat reſtored vnto ioye ſhe deſired ſhe might firſt ſhutte chāber doore leaſt vntemperance tongue vtteringe vnſittinge woordes might growe inconuenience wherewithall ſhe barred propped doore came againe embraſing louingly necke armes ſpake wt ſofte voice ſaide doo greatly feare diſcouer priuities houſe vtter ſecrete miſteries dame haue ſuche confidence wiſedome reaſon ar come ſo noble ligne endewed ſo profounde ſapience enſtructed ſo many holy diuine thinges faithfully kéepe ſilence ſo euer ſhall reueale declare vnto woulde cloſe within bottome hart neuer diſcouer ſame enſure loue beare vnto enforceth vtter ſhall knowe eſtate houſe nowe ſhall knowe hidden ſecreates miſtris vnto whome power hell doo obaye whome celeſtiall planettes troubled goddes made weake element ſubdued neither violence arte ſtrength force ſhe eſpieth ſome comely yonge man pleaſeth fancie oftētimes happeneth nowe ſhe loueth one beotian fayre beautifull perſon whome ſhe employeth ſorcery enchauntment harde ſay mine owne eares yeſternight sunne preſently gone downe hight come miniſter conuenient time woorke magicall enticementes ſhe would haue brought perpetuall darknes ouer worlde ſelf ſhall know ſhe ſaw yeſternight beotian ſittinge barbours polinge ſhe came baines ſhe ſecretely cōmaunded gather ſome heare head whiche lay diſperſed vpon grounde bringe honie whiche thought haue done barbour eſpied reaſon bruted thorough citie weare witch enchantreſſes cried ſaid neuer leaue ſtealinge yonge men heares faith aſſure vnleſſe ceaſe wicked ſorceries complaine y• iuſtices wherwithall came angerly towardes toke away heare whiche gathered mine apron whiche grieued muche knew miſtris manner ſhe would contented beate cruelly wherfore entended runne away remembrance put alwaies thought minde ſo came homewarde ſorowfull becauſe would ſéeme come miſtris ſight emptie handes ſawe man ſhearynge blowen goate ſkinnes heare ſhorne yellow much reſembled heare beotian toke good deale thereof colouringe matter brought miſtris ſo night came retorne frō ſupper ſhe bringe purpoſe paſſe wente vp high gallery houſe openyng eaſt parte worlde preparinge ſelfe accordinge accuſtomed practiſe ſhe gathered together ſubſtance fumigatiōs ſhe brought forth plate mettall carued ſtraunge charecters ſhe prepared bone ſuch drowned tempeſt ſeas ſhe made reddy mēbers dead men noſethrilles finger ſette lumpes fleſh ſuche weare hanged bloudde whiche ſhe reſerued ſuch weare ſlaine iawe bone téeth wilde beaſtes ſhe ſaid certaine charmes ouer heare dipped diuers water well water cowe milke mountaine hony licour whiche ſhe done ſhe tied lapped vp together many perfume ſmelles threw whote fire burne great force ſorcerie violence ſo many confection thoſe body whoſe heare burnyng fire receaued humaine ſhape felte hard walked ſmellinge ſent owne heare came rappid doores ſtéede boetius thē beinge well tippled deceaued obſcuritie night drewe ſwoorde couragiouſly like furious aiax killed whole hearde beaſtes thrée blowen ſkinnes intent ſlaughter ſo many enemy without effuſiō bloud might embrace kiſſe homicide vtricide thus pleaſantly mocked taunted fotis ſaid vnto verely may atchieued enterpriſe numbred hercules valiaunt proweſſe perfourmed twelue notable labour gerion thrée body cerberus thrée heades haue ſ • aine thrée blowen geate ſkinnes ende may pardon thée whiche thou haſt committed performe thinge whiche ſhall moſt earneſtly deſire thée bringe may ſée beholde thy miſtris goeth sorcerie enchauntment ſhe prayeth vnto goddes verie deſirous learne arte ſéemeth vnto thou thy ſelfe haſte ſome experience ſame knowe plainely féele whereas haue alwaies yrked lothed embraſinges loue matrones ſo ſtryken ſubdued thy ſhininge eye ruddy chéekes glitteringe heare ſwéete coſſes lillie white pappes neither haue minde goe home departe henſe eſtéeme pleaſure whiche ſhall haue thée night aboue ioyes worlde ꝙ ſhe lucius willinge would fulfill deſire reaſon ſhe ſo hated ſhe getteth ſelfe ſolitary place preſence euerie perſon ſhe mindeth woorke enchantmentes regarde gratifie requeſt doo eſtéeme daunger life ſée oportunitie time wil aſſuredly bring woorde ſo ſhall ſée enchauntment alwaies vpon condicion ye ſecreately keepe cloſe ſuche thinges done thus reaſoned together courage venus aſſayled aſwell deſires member ſo ſhe vnrayed ſelfe came bedde paſſed nighte paſtime dalliance till drowſie vnluſtie ſléepe conſtrained lie ſtill ¶howe fotis brought apuleius ſee miſtris enchaunt cap 16 day fotis came runninge great feare ſaide miſtris worke ſorceries ſuch ſhe loued entēded night followinge tranſforme ſelfe birde flie whither ſhe pleaſed wherefore ſhe willed priuily prepare ſelfe ſée ſame whē midnight came ſhe ledde ſoftly highe chamber bidde looke thorough chinke doore firſte ſaw ſhe put garmentes toke certaine coffer ſondrie kinde box ſhe opened one tempred ointment therin finger rubbed bodie therewith frō ſole foote crowne head ſhe ſpoken priuilie ſelfe hauinge candle hande ſhe ſhaked partes bodie beholde perceaued plume feather burgen noſe waxed croked harde nailes turned clawes ſo ſhe became owle ſhe cried ſkriched like birde kinde willinge proue force moued ſelfe groūd litle litle till laſt ſhe flewe quight away thus sorcery ſhe tranſformed body ſhape ſhe wold whē ſaw greatly aſtonied although enchaunted kinde charme yet thought y• ſéemed haue y• likenes luciꝰ ſo baniſhed frō ſenſes amaſed madnes ſo dreamed wakinge y• felte mine eies know whether weare ſléepe whē come againe ſelfe toke fotis y• hāde moued face ſaid pray thée occaſion doth ſerue may haue fruition fruictes deſire graunt ſome ointment fotis praye thy ſwéete pappes make great flame loue may turned birde ſo euer hereafter boūde vnto obedient commaundement ſaid fotis goe deceaue enforce worke mine owne ſorrowe minde tarry theſſalie birde ſhal ſeeke ſhal ſee anſweared god forbidde ſhould commit ſuch crime though could flie y• ayre egle though meſſenger iupiter yet would haue recourſe neſt thee ſweare knotte thy amiable heare ſince time firſte loued thée neuer fancied perſon moreouer commeth minde vertue ointment ſhall become owle take héede come nigh man houſe learne theſe matrones would handle louers knewe tranſformed owles moreouer taken place nayled vpon poſtes ſo woorthely rewarded becauſe thought bringe euill fortune houſe pray whiche almoſt forgotten tell meanes owle ſhall returne priſtine ſhape become lucius againe feare ꝙ ſhe miſtris hath taught way bringe paſſe neither thinke 〈◊〉 ſhe good fauour ende might helpe miniſter ſome remedie ſhe • urneth home conſider pray ſelfe friu • lous trifle ſo meruelous thinge wrought hercules ſweare giue harde finger toe leſing nūber fiue chaunged hoofes mine arſe grewe great taile face became monſtruous noſethrilles wide lippes hanginge downe mine eares rugged heare neither could ſée comfort aduerſitie good parte went y• ſtable mine ownehorſe found aſſe miloes ſomtime mine hoſte verely thinke mine owne horſe natural cōſciēce knowledge brute beaſtes would take pitie vpō proffer lodging rafter ſtable image goddeſſe hippone whiche garniſhed decked rounde faire freſh roſes hope preſent remedie leaped vp fore féete highe coulde ſtretchinge necke lippes coueted ſnatche ſome roſes euill poore wretch vntil ſuch time great noyes rumbling harde doores houſe burſt open neighbour cry lamentable ſorte whiche enforced ſtroken feare flie way troope théeues entred kepte euery parte corner houſe weapon men reſorted ayde helpe thē weare within doores théeues reſiſted kept backe euery man armed ſwoorde targette hande glympſes whereof yelde ſuch light bene daye brake opē great cheſte double locke boltes wherein laide treaſure milo ranſakt ſame done packed vp gaue euery one porciō carry could beare away yet weare lothe leaue behinde came ſtable toke v twoo poore aſſes horſe laded v greater truſſes weare able beare weare houſe followed v great ſtaues willed one fellowes tarry behinde bringe tidinges done concerninge robbery ſo beate v forwarde ouer great hilles y• high way heauy burthen longe iourney nothinge differ dead aſſe wherfore determined ſelfe ſéeke ſome ciuill remedie inuocation name prince countrie deliuered ſo many miſeries time paſſed thorough great faire came amongſt multitude gréekes thought call vpon renoumed name emperour ſay ceſar cried aloude ceſar could wiſe pronounce théeues little regardinge criynge lay beate wretched ſkinne ſuch ſorte neither apte méete make ſiues ſarces laſte iupiter miniſterd vnto vnhoped remedie paſſed thorough many townes village fortuned eſpie pleaſaunt garden wherein beſides many flower delectable hewe weare newe freſhe roſes beinge ioyfull deſirous catche ſome paſſed drewe nerer nerer lippes watred vpō thought better aduiſe profitable leaſt aſſe ſhould become man might fal hādes theeues either ſuſpitiō weare ſome witche feare would vtter thefte ſhould ſlaine wherfore abſtained time frō eatinge roſes enduringe preſent aduerſitie eate hay aſſes fourth booke lucius apuleius golden aſſe ¶how apuleius thinkinge goe eate roſes cruelly beaten gardener chaſed dogges cap 18 noone come broylinge heate sunne moſte power turned village certaine théeues acquaintāce fréendes verely metinge embraſinge together giue poore aſſe cauſe déeme ye ſame thei toke truſſe backe gaue parte treaſure whiche séemed whiſper tel ſtolen goodes weare vnladen burthen thei lette v loſe medow paſture mine owne horſe milo aſſe would ſuffer féede muſte ſéeke dinner ſome place wherefore leaped gardein whiche behinde ſtable beinge welnie periſhed honger although could finde nothing raw gréene ſallettes yet filled hongry guttes therewithall abundantly praying vnto goddes loked euery place could eſpie redde roſes garden ſolitarie alone put good hope y• could finde remedie ſhould preſently aſſe chaunged lucius euery man ſight conſidered theſe thinges looked behold ſaw farre ſhadowed valley adioyninge nigh vnto woodde emongſt diuers hearbes pleaſaunt verdure thought ſawe many floriſhinge roſes bright damaſke colour ſaid within beſtiall minde verely y• place place venus grace ſecretely glittereth royall hewe liuely delectable flower deſiring y• helpe guide good fortune ranne luſtely towardes woodde ſo much y• felt ſelf aſſe ſwifte courſinge horſe agilitie quicknes could preuent crueltie fortune came place perceaued roſes neither tēder pleaſant neither moiſted heauenly droppes dew celeſtiall licour whiche grewe thicket thornes neither perceaue y• valley onely banke riuer enuironed great thicke trées lōg braūches like vnto lawrel bearinge flower without manner ſente common people call name lawrell roſes whiche poyſon manner beaſtes ſo entangled vnhappy fortune litle eſtéemed mine owne daunger went willingly eate thoſe roſes though knewe preſent poyſon drewe nere ſawe yong man ſéemed gardener come vpon perceaued deuoured vp hearbes gardein came ſwearinge great ſtaffe hande laide vpon ſuch ſorte welnie dead ſpéedely deuiſed ſome remedy ſelfe lifte vp legges kicked hinder héeles lefte liynge hill foote welnie ſlaine ſo ranne away incontinently came wife ſeinge huſbande halfe dead cried houled pitifull ſorte wente towarde huſbande intent lowde cry ſhe might purchaſe preſent deſtruction thē perſons towne moued rayſed noyes came foorth cried dogges teare downe came great company bandogges maſties fitte pull downe beares lion behelde thought verely ſhould preſently die turned ſelfe aboute ranne faſte euer might ſtable frō whenſe came men towne called dogges toke bounde ſtaple poſte ſcourged great knotted whippe till welny dead would vndoubtedly haue ſlaine come paſſe paine beatinge gréene hearbes lay guttes caught ſuche laſke ſprinkled face liquide donge enforced leaue ¶how apuleius preuented purpoſe theeues came denne cap 19 longe théeues laded v againe eſpecially brought v foorth ſtable gone good parte iourney longe way great burthen beatinge ſtaues worne hoofes ſo weary could ſcantly goe ſawe litle riuer runninge faire water ſaid ſelfe behold haue founde good occaſiō fall downe come yender ſurely riſe againe neither ſcourginge beatinge rather ſlaine preſently goe cauſe determined ſo doo thought théeues ſée ſo féeble weake could trauell intent would ſtay iourney would take burthen backe put vpon fellowes ſo puniſhment leaue praye wolues rauenous beaſtes euill fortune preuented ſo good conſideration aſſe beinge ſame purpoſe feigned coloured werines fell downe firſt burthen vpon grounde though weare dead would riſe neither beatinge prickinge ſtande vpon féete though pulled vp taile legges eares whiche théeues behelde without al hope ſaid one ſhould ſtande ſo longe dead rather ſtony aſſe let v gonne ſo thei toke burthen deuided ſome ſome horſe drewe ſwoordes cutte legges threwe bodie pointe hill downe great valley conſidering ſelfe euill fortune poore compaignion purpoſed forgette al ſubtiltie deceite play good aſſe gette maiſters fauour perceaued talke weare welny come home iourneis end paſſed ouer litle hil came appointed place whē weare vnladen burthen thinges carried tumbled wallowed duſt refreſh ſelfe ſtéede water thing time cō pelleth make deſcription place ſpecially denne théeues inhabite wil proue witte doo conſider whether aſſe iudgement ſenſe firſt excéeding great hill compaſſed bigge trées high many turning bottomes full ſharpe ſtones whereby inacceſſible many windinge hollow valleis enuironed thickettes thornes naturally fortreſſed round frō toppe hill ranne runninge riuer cléere ſiluer watred valeis ſéemed like vnto ſea encloſed ſtandinge floode denne hill ſtoode highe towre foote thereof weare ſhepecotes fenced watled clay gate houſe pathes made ſtéede walles ſuch ſorte would eaſely iudge denne théeues nothinge elſe ſaue litle coate couered thatche wherein théeues nightly accuſtome watch order perceaued crepte houſe faſte tied halter doore began chide olde woman crooked age gouernment rule al houſe ſaid olde witche olde trotte ſtrumpet thou ſitteſt idely day home hauinge regarde perillous labor haſte prouided nothinge ſuppers ſitteſt eating ſwillinge thy ſelfe morning til night old woman trembled ſcantly able ſpeake gan ſay beholde puiſant faithful maiſters ſhal haue meate potage inough firſt ſtore bread wine plentie filled cleane rinſed pottes likewiſe whote water prepared bathe whiche ſhe ſaid put garmentes refreſhed ſelues fire thei waſhed nointed oyle ſatte downe table garniſhed kinde deinty meates thei ſooner ſet downe came company yonge men number ſéemed likewiſe théeues thei brought praies golde siluer plate iuelles riche robe likewiſe waſhed ſatte emōgſt reſt ſerued one ordre thē thei dranke eate excedingly criyng laughing making ſuch noyes y• thought emongſt tirannous wilde lapithes thebanes centaures length one thē valiant reſt ſpake ſorte verely haue manfully cōquered houſe milo hypata beſide richeſſe treaſure force haue brought away come home ſalue encreaſed horſe aſſe haue roued countrey beotia haue loſte valiant capitaine lamathus whoſe life regarded treaſure haue brought therefore memorie ſhalbe renoumed euer emongſt moſte noble kinges valiant capitaines accuſtome goe abroade like men gander harte créepe euery corner hole euery trifle one came laſte anſweared onely ignorant greater number ſooner may robbe ſpoyle houſe although familie diſperſed diuers lodginges yet euery man rather defende owne life ſaue richeſſe maiſter fewe théeues rather onely regarde ſelues alſo ſubſtāce litle great ſo euer intent may beléeue wil ſhow example weare come nothinge nighe vnto thebe fountaine arte ſciēce learned riche chuffe called chryſeros dwell feare office y• publique weale diſſimuled eſtate liued ſole ſolitary ſmall cote repleniſhed aboundaunce treaſure wente dayly ragged torne apparell wherefore deuiſed ſelues goe houſe ſpoyle richeſſe whē night came drew towardes doore ſo ſtrōgly cloſed y• could neither moue lifte y• hooke thought beſt breake open leaſt y• noyes ſhould raiſe vp harme neighbor bie ſtronge valiant capitaine lamathus truſtinge owne ſtrength force thruſt hāde hole doore thought pull backe bolte couetous caytife chryſeros beinge awake making noyes came ſoftely doore caught hande great naile nailed faſt poſte donne ranne vp high chāber called euery one neighbour name deſiringe ſuccour poſſible ſpéede houſe fire euery one feare owne daunger came runninge ayde wherewith fearinge preſent perill knewe beſt done whether ſhould leaue compaignion yelde ſelues die conſent deuiſed better way cut arme elbow ſo let hange there▪ boūd wound cloutes leaſt ſhould traced droppes bloud done tooke lamathus ledde away feare ſhould taken weare ſo nighe purſued weare preſent daunger lamathus coulde kéepe companie reaſon faintnes y• ſide perceauinge profite linger behinde ſpake vnto v man ſinguler courage vertue deſiringe v much entreatie prayer puiſance god mar faith confederacie deliuer bodie torment miſerable captiuitie ſaid poſſible ſo couragious capitaine liue without hand wherwith could ſomtimes robbe ſlea ſo many people would thinke ſelfe ſufficient happy might ſlaine one whē ſaw refuſed cōmitte ſuch facte drewe ſwoorde hande often kiſſed thruſt cleane thorough bodie honored corp ſo puiſant man wrapped linnen clothes threw ſea ſo lieth maſter lamathus buried hidde graue water ended life haue declared alcinus though weare man great enterpriſe yet could beware lamathus volde ſelfe euil fortune day entred olde woman houſe robbe went vp high chāber ſhould firſt haue ſtrāgled regarde throw downe bagges money golde window v ſtoode vnder ſo gréedie would leaue nothinge behinde went olde woman bedde ſhe lay ſléepe would haue taken couerlet haue throwē downe likewiſe ſhe awaked knelyng vpon knées deſired manner ſir pray caſte away ſuche torne ragged clouſes neighbour houſes riche inough néede ſuch thinges alcinus thinking woordes true brought beliefe ſuch thinges throwen already ſuch thinges ſhould throwe fallen downe fellowes men houſes wherfore went window ſée thought beholde place rounde thruſtinge bodie window old womā marked well came behinde ſoftlie although ſhe ſmall ſtrength yet ſodaine force ſhe tooke héeles thruſt headlonge ſo fell vpon meruelous great ſtone burſt ribbes whereby vomited ſpued flake bloud preſently died threw riuer likewiſe done lamathus thus loſt twoo compaignions liked thebe marched towardes next citie called platea founde mā great fame named demochares purpoſed ſet foorth great game ſhould triall al kinde weapon come good houſe meruelous riche liberall well deſerued prepared many ſhowes pleaſures common people ſo much mā either witte eloquence ſhowe woordes woorthy preparatiōs firſt prouided ſortes armes greatly delighted huntinge chaſinge ordeyned great towres table moue hither thither made many place chaſe encounter ready great number men wilde beaſtes many cō demned perſons brought iudgement place trie fight thoſe beaſtes emongſt ſo great preparation noble pryce beſtowed moſte parte patrimonie biynge beares whiche nouriſhed great coſte eſtéemed beaſtes eitheir chaſinge caught ſelfe whiche déerely bought giuen diuers fréendes howbeit al ſumptuous coſte could frée frō malitious eies enuie ſome welnie dead longe tiynge vp ſome meigre broyling heate sunne ſome lāguiſhed liynge hauinge ſundry diſeaſes weare ſo afflicted taht died one welnie none lefte ſuch ſorte might ſée liyng ſtréetes piteouſly dead common people hauing meate féede litle regardinge curioſitie would come foorth fill belly fleaſh beares babulus deuiſed pretie ſporte drewe one greateſt beares lodging though would prepare eate thereof fleade ſkinne kepte vngles whole medled head cutte necke ſo let hange ſkinne raſed fleaſh backe caſt duſt thereon ſet sunne drie ¶how thraſileon diſguiſed beares ſkinne handled cap 20 ſkinne driynge made mery fleaſhe deuiſed ſelues one v valiant reſt bothe bodie courage ſo would conſent thereto ſhoulde put ſkinne feminge weare beare ſhould ledde demochares houſe night whiche meanes thought receaued lette many deſirous play beare eſpecially one thraſileon couragious minde would take enterpriſe hande put beares ſkinne whiche fitted finely euery pointe buckled faſt vnder belly couered ſeame heare y• might ſéene made litle hole thorough beares head thorough noſethrilles cies thraſileon ſée take winde ſuch ſorte ſéemed liuely naturall beaſt demochares wherein wrote ſent fréende firſt fruictes courſing huntinge night come whiche méete time purpoſe brought thraſileon forged letter preſented thē demochares demochares behelde mightie beare ſaw liberalitie nicanor fréende cōmaunded ſeruaunt deliuer vnto v tenne crownes great ſtore coffer noueltie thing doth accuſtome ſtirre men mindes beholde ſame many perſons came euery ſide ſée beare thraſileō leſt ſhould curious viewyng priyng perceaue truthe ranne vpon put feare thei durſt come nie people ſaid verely demochares right happy death ſo many beaſtes hath gotten maugre fortune head ſo goodly beare demochares commaunded great care ſhould put parke emongſt beaſtes immediatly ſpake vnto ſaid sir pray take héede put beaſte tyred heate sunne longe trauell emongſt others whiche ſay haue diuers malady diſeaſes let rather lie ſome opē place houſe nighe ſome water may take ayre eaſe ſelfe doo know ſuche kinde beaſtes doo greatly delight ot couche vnder ſhadow trées hillockes nigh vnto pleaſant welles water hereby demochares admoniſhed remembringe many periſhed contented ſhould put beare would moreouer ſaide vnto ſelues wre determined lie night nigh vnto beare looke vnto giue meate drinke due hower anſweared verely maiſters néede put ſelues ſuch paine haue men taht ſerueth nothinge purpoſe ſo toke leaue departed weare come without gate towne perceaued v great sepulchre ſtandinge highe way priuie ſecreate place thither wente opened mouth thereof whereas founde ſides couered corruption man aſhes duſt longe buried bodie wherein gotte ſelues bringe purpoſe paſſe hauinge reſpect darke time night accordinge cuſtome thought euery man ſléepe went weapōs beſieged houſe demochares round thraſileon reddy hande leaped cauerne wente kill ſuch founde ſléepe came porter opened gate let v thē ſhowed v large counter wherin ſawe put night great aboundaunce treaſure whiche violence broken open bidde euery one fellowes take much golde siluer could beare away carry sepulchre ſtill caried ſtoode gate watchinge diligently would retorne beare runned houſe make ſuch familie affeard fortuned wake come ſo puiſant courageous vgly ſight ſo great monſter quaile kéepe chamber eſpecially night brought matter ſo good pointe chaunced pitiful caſe looked compaignions ſhould come sepulchre beholde boye houſe fortuned looke windowe eſpied beare rūning went tolde al ſeruaūtes houſe whereupon incontinently came foorth torch lanthornes lightes might ſée yarde ouer thei came clubbes ſpeares naked ſwoordes greyhoundes maſties ſlea poore beaſt duringe broile thought runne away becauſe would ſée thraſileon fightinge dogges lay behinde y• gate beholde although might perceaue welnie dead yet remembred owne faithfulnes valiātly reſiſted gaping rauenous mouthes helhoūdes ſo toke grée pageant willingly toke hande ſelfe much doo tumbled length houſe libertie abroade yet coulde ſaue ſelfe dogges ſtreate ioyned ſelues greyhoūdes maſties houſe came vpon ala pitifull ſight poor thraſileon thus enuironed compassed ſo many dogges tare rente miſerably impatient ſo great miſerie rāne emongſt preaſe people ayding woordes much might exhorted al manner great extreame miſchaunce pretious excellent beaſt haue loſte woordes nothinge preuaile came tale man ſpeare hande yt truſt cleane thorough afterwardes many ſtoode drewe ſwoordes killed verely good capitaine thraſileon honour cōforte receaued death ſo patiently would bewray league betwene v either criynge howlinge meanes torne dogges wounded weapon yelde foorth dolefull crie like vnto beaſt mā takinge preſent fortune good parte courage glory inough finiſh life ſuch terrour vnto aſſembly perſon ſo hardy vntill day touch though weare ſtarke dead laſt came butcher valiant reſt openinge panche beaſt ſlitte hardy venturous théefe manner loſte capitaine thraſileon▪ loſt fame honour done packed vp treaſure cōmitted sepulchre kéepe gotte v boundes platea thinkinge ſelues fidelitie emongeſt dead emōgſt liuing reaſon praies ſo ſurely kept sepulchre weried weight burthen welnie tired long trauel hauing loſt thrée ſouldiours come home theſe preſent cheates thus whē ſpoken memory ſlaine cōpaignions thei tooke cuppes golde ſonge hympnes vnto god mar layde downe ſléepe old woman gaue v freſh barley without meaſure ſo much horſe ſedde ſo abundantly might well thinke ſome bankette day accuſtomed eate branne flowre thought ſower kinde meate wherfore eſpiyng corner lay loues bread houſe gotte thither filled hungry guttes withall ¶how theeues ſtole away gentel woman brought denne cap 21 night come théeues awaked roſe vp thei buckled weapōs diſguiſed face viſardes departed yet al great ſléepe y• came vpon could wiſe leaue eatinge wheras man could cōtented wt one twoo loues moſt carefull heauy bringinge burthen ſo muche traffe baggage ſaue onely maiden ſéemed habite ſome gētle woman borne daughter ſome woorthy matron countrey ſo faire beautifull though weare aſſe yet great affection virgin lamented tare heare ſpoyled garmentes great ſorrow ſhe théeues brought within caue aſſaied cō ſorte ſorte wéepe fayre gentle woman pray aſſured wil doo outrage violence perſon take pacience profit neceſſitie poore eſtate hath cōpelled v doo enterpriſe warrant parentes although couetous wil contented giue v great quātitie money redéeme ranſom handes ſuch like flattering woordes endeuored appeaſe gentle woman ſhe would caſe comforted put head betwene knées cried piteouſly thei called old woman commaunded sitte maiden pacifie dolor much ſhe might departed away robbe accuſtomed doo virgin would aſſwage griefes mitigate ſorrow entreatie olde woman houled ſobbed ſuch ſorte ſhe made poore aſſe likewiſe wéepe thus ſhe ſaid ala poore wretche liue longer come ſo good houſe forſaken al parentes fréendes familie made rapine pray cloſed ſeruily ſtony priſon depriued pleaſure wherein haue bene brought vp throwen daūger ready rente péeces emongeſt ſo many ſturdy théeues dreadfull robber ſay ceaſe wepinge liue lenger thus ſhe cried lamē ted ſhe weried ſelfe ſorrow bloubered face teares ſhe cloſed y• windowes hollow eies laide downe ſléepe taht ſhe ſlept ſhe roſe againe like furious madde woman beate breaſt comely face ſhe old woman enquired cauſes newe ſodaine lamentation ſighing pitifull ſorte ſhe anſweared ala vtterly vndone hope giue knife kill halter hoare head ſome calamitie comely yonge man bountie grace beloued entierly towne cooſin germaine thrée yeres elder twoo nouriſhed brought vp one houſe lay vnder one roofe one chamber lengthe promiſe thy perill goe aboute thy affayres carefull leaſt harme ſhould happen vnto thée credibly informed neither vtter vnto thée great serpent full deadly poyſon rauenous gapinge threate lieth thée euery night remember oracle apollo pronounced thou ſhouldeſt married dyre • erte serpent many inhabitantes ſuch hunte countrey affirme ſawe yeſternight returnynge paſture ſwimminge ouer riuer whereby doo vndoubtedly ſay pamper thée longe delicate meates time deliuerie ſhall approche deuoure thée thy childe wherfore aduiſe thy ſelfe whether thou wilt agrée vnto v carefull thy ſafetie ſo auoide perill death contented liue thy ſiſters whether thou wilt remaine ſerpent ende ſwallowed gowlfe bodie ſo thy ſolitary life thy conuerſation voyces ſeruile daungerous pleaſure loue serpent doo delight thée ſay haue playde partes naturall ſiſters warninge thée poore ſimple miſer pſyches moued feare ſo dreadfull woordes amaſed minde cleane forgette admonition huſbande owne promiſes made vnto throwyng good way diſtant citie perceaued delicate meates libertie ſhould hauevnhappy hath ill miſtris couetous wife moſt curſed queane made mill aſſe beatinge kidgell full knottes would wringe bredde ſelf would thereby fat better fleſhe knowe ſelfe well many aſſes alſo moſte fierce horſes reaſon wantonnes haue bene moſt madde terrible weare gelded cut haue become gentle tame tractable vſe wherfore
